	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Bay of Pigs Invasion</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
		<div id="contentSub"></div>
		
		
		
		<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>

		<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">"Invasion of Cuba" redirects here. For the British invasion in 1741, see <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Cuba_(1741)" title="Invasion of Cuba (1741)">Invasion of Cuba (1741)</a>.</div>
<div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Failed U.S.sponsored invasion of Cuba, 1961</div>

</p>

<td><a href="/wiki/Timber_Sycamore" title="Timber Sycamore">2012–2017 Syria, Timber Sycamore</a>
<br /><div class="plainlinks hlist navbar" style="float:right;"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Covert_United_States_involvement_in_regime_change" title="Template:Covert United States involvement in regime change"><span title="View this template">view</span></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Covert_United_States_involvement_in_regime_change" title="Template talk:Covert United States involvement in regime change"><span title="Discuss this template">talk</span></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Covert_United_States_involvement_in_regime_change&amp;action=edit"><span title="Edit this template">edit</span></a></li></ul></div>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The <b>Bay of Pigs Invasion</b> (Spanish: <b>Invasión de Playa Girón</b> or <b>Invasión de Bahía de Cochinos</b> or <b>Batalla de Girón</b>) was a failed military invasion of <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a> undertaken by the <a href="/wiki/Central_Intelligence_Agency" title="Central Intelligence Agency">Central Intelligence Agency</a> (CIA)-sponsored rebel group <a href="/wiki/Brigade_2506" title="Brigade 2506">Brigade 2506</a> on 17 April 1961. A counter-revolutionary military group (made up of mostly Cuban exiles who had traveled to the United States after Castro's takeover, but also some <a href="/wiki/United_States_Armed_Forces" title="United States Armed Forces">US military</a> personnel<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>), trained and funded by the CIA, Brigade 2506 fronted the armed wing of the <a href="/wiki/Cuban_Democratic_Revolutionary_Front" title="Cuban Democratic Revolutionary Front">Democratic Revolutionary Front</a> (DRF) and intended to overthrow the <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Cuba" title="Politics of Cuba">increasingly communist government</a> of <a href="/wiki/Fidel_Castro" title="Fidel Castro">Fidel Castro</a>. Launched from <a href="/wiki/Guatemala" title="Guatemala">Guatemala</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nicaragua" title="Nicaragua">Nicaragua</a>, the invading force was defeated within three days by the <a href="/wiki/Cuban_Revolutionary_Armed_Forces" title="Cuban Revolutionary Armed Forces">Cuban Revolutionary Armed Forces</a>, under the direct command of Castro.
</p><p>The coup of 1952 led by General <a href="/wiki/Fulgencio_Batista" title="Fulgencio Batista">Fulgencio Batista</a>, an ally of the United States, against President <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Pr%C3%ADo_Socarr%C3%A1s" title="Carlos Prío Socarrás">Carlos Prio</a>, forced him to take exile in <a href="/wiki/Miami" title="Miami">Miami</a>. Prio's exile was the reason for the <a href="/wiki/26th_July_Movement" class="mw-redirect" title="26th July Movement">26th July Movement</a> led by Castro. The movement, which did not succeed until after the Cuban Revolution of 31 December 1958, severed the country's formerly strong links with the US after nationalizing American industrial assets (banks, oil refineries, sugar and coffee plantations) along with other American owned businesses.
</p><p>It was after the <a href="/wiki/Cuban_Revolution" title="Cuban Revolution">Cuban Revolution</a> of 1959 that Castro forged strong economic links with the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> whom the United States primarily engaged in the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>. US President <a href="/wiki/Dwight_D._Eisenhower" title="Dwight D. Eisenhower">Dwight D. Eisenhower</a> was very concerned at the direction Castro's government was taking, and in March 1960 he allocated $13.1 million to the CIA to plan Castro's overthrow. The CIA proceeded to organize the operation with the aid of various Cuban counter-revolutionary forces, training Brigade 2506 in Guatemala. Eisenhower's successor, <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy" title="John F. Kennedy">John F. Kennedy</a>, approved the final invasion plan on 4 April 1961.
</p><p>Over 1,400 paramilitaries, divided into five infantry battalions and one paratrooper battalion, assembled in Guatemala before setting out for Cuba by boat on 13 April 1961. Two days later, on 15 April, eight CIA-supplied <a href="/wiki/Douglas_A-26_Invader" title="Douglas A-26 Invader">B-26</a> bombers attacked Cuban airfields and then returned to the US. On the night of 16 April, the main invasion landed at a beach named <a href="/wiki/Playa_Gir%C3%B3n" title="Playa Girón">Playa Girón</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Pigs" title="Bay of Pigs">Bay of Pigs</a>. It initially overwhelmed a local revolutionary militia. The Cuban Army's counter-offensive was led by <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Ram%C3%B3n_Fern%C3%A1ndez" title="José Ramón Fernández">José Ramón Fernández</a> before Castro decided to take personal control of the operation. As the US involvement became apparent to the world, and with the initiative turning against the invasion, Kennedy decided against providing further air cover.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> As a result, the operation only had half the forces the CIA had deemed necessary. The original plan devised during Eisenhower's presidency had required both air and naval support. On 20 April, the invaders surrendered after only three days, with the majority being publicly interrogated and put into Cuban prisons.
</p><p>The failed invasion helped to strengthen the position of Castro's leadership, made him a national hero, and entrenched the rocky relationship between the former allies. It also reinforced the relations between Cuba and the Soviet Union. Strengthened Soviet-Cuban relations eventually led to the events of the <a href="/wiki/Cuban_Missile_Crisis" title="Cuban Missile Crisis">Cuban Missile Crisis</a> of 1962. The invasion was a significant failure for Kennedy's <a href="/wiki/US_foreign_policy" class="mw-redirect" title="US foreign policy">US foreign policy</a>.
</p>

</div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Background">Background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bay_of_Pigs_Invasion&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Since the middle of the 18th century, Cuba had been the crown jewel of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish colonial empire</a>. In the late 19th century, Cuban nationalist revolutionaries rebelled against Spanish dominance, resulting in three liberation wars: the <a href="/wiki/Ten_Years%27_War" title="Ten Years&#39; War">Ten Years' War</a> (1868–1878), the <a href="/wiki/Little_War_(Cuba)" title="Little War (Cuba)">Little War</a> (1879–1880) and the <a href="/wiki/Cuban_War_of_Independence" title="Cuban War of Independence">Cuban War of Independence</a> (1895–1898). The United States government proclaimed war on the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish Empire</a>, resulting in the <a href="/wiki/Spanish%E2%80%93American_War" title="Spanish–American War">Spanish–American War</a> (1898). The US subsequently invaded the island and forced the Spanish army out. Of note, a special operations attempt to land a group of at least 375 Cuban soldiers on the island succeeded in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Tayacoba" title="Battle of Tayacoba">Battle of Tayacoba</a> of the Spanish–American War. On 20 May 1902, a new independent government proclaimed the foundation of the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Cuba" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of Cuba">Republic of Cuba</a>, with US Military governor <a href="/wiki/Leonard_Wood" title="Leonard Wood">Leonard Wood</a> handing over control to President <a href="/wiki/Tom%C3%A1s_Estrada_Palma" title="Tomás Estrada Palma">Tomás Estrada Palma</a>, a Cuban-born US citizen.<sup id="cite_ref-Gott_113_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gott_113-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Subsequently, large numbers of US settlers and businessmen arrived in Cuba, and by 1905, 60% of rural properties were owned by non-Cuban North Americans.<sup id="cite_ref-Gott_115_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gott_115-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Between 1906 and 1909, 5,000 US Marines were stationed across the island, and returned in 1912, 1917 and 1921 to intervene in internal affairs, sometimes at the behest of the Cuban government.<sup id="cite_ref-Gott_115-116_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gott_115-116-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fidel_Castro_and_the_Cuban_Revolution">Fidel Castro and the Cuban Revolution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bay_of_Pigs_Invasion&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Fidel Castro and the Cuban Revolution">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="quotebox pullquote floatright" style="width:25em;&#32;; background-color: #ACE1AF;"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r887775652">.mw-parser-output .quotebox{background-color:#F9F9F9;border:1px solid #aaa;box-sizing:border-box;padding:10px;font-size:88%;max-width:100%}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft{margin:0.5em 1.4em 0.8em 0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright{margin:0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.centered{margin:0.5em auto 0.8em auto}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft p,.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright p{font-style:inherit}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-title{background-color:#F9F9F9;text-align:center;font-size:larger;font-weight:bold}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:before{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" “ ";vertical-align:-45%;line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:after{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" ” ";line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .left-aligned{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .right-aligned{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .center-aligned{text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .quotebox cite{display:block;font-style:normal}@media screen and (max-width:360px){.mw-parser-output .quotebox{min-width:100%;margin:0 0 0.8em!important;float:none!important}}</style>
<div class="quotebox-quote left-aligned" style="">Until Castro, the US was so overwhelmingly influential in Cuba that the American ambassador was the second most important man, sometimes even more important than the Cuban president.</div>
<p><cite class="left-aligned" style="">— <a href="/wiki/Earl_E._T._Smith" title="Earl E. T. Smith">Earl E. T. Smith</a>, former American Ambassador to Cuba, during 1960 testimony to the US Senate<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup></cite>
</p>
</div>
<p>In March 1952, a Cuban general and politician, <a href="/wiki/Fulgencio_Batista" title="Fulgencio Batista">Fulgencio Batista</a>, seized power on the island, proclaimed himself president and deposed the discredited president <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Pr%C3%ADo_Socarr%C3%A1s" title="Carlos Prío Socarrás">Carlos Prío Socarrás</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Partido_Aut%C3%A9ntico" title="Partido Auténtico">Partido Auténtico</a>. Batista canceled the planned presidential elections, and described his new system as "disciplined democracy." Although Batista gained some popular support, many Cubans saw it as the establishment of a one-man dictatorship.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Many opponents of the Batista regime took to armed rebellion in an attempt to oust the government, sparking the <a href="/wiki/Cuban_Revolution" title="Cuban Revolution">Cuban Revolution</a>. One of these groups was the National Revolutionary Movement (<i>Movimiento Nacional Revolucionario</i> – MNR), a militant organization containing largely middle-class members that had been founded by the Professor of Philosophy <a href="/wiki/Rafael_Garc%C3%ADa_B%C3%A1rcena" title="Rafael García Bárcena">Rafael García Bárcena</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> Another was the <a href="/wiki/Directorio_Revolucionario_Estudantil" class="mw-redirect" title="Directorio Revolucionario Estudantil">Directorio Revolucionario Estudantil</a> (DRE), which had been founded by the Federation of University Students (FEU) President <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Antonio_Echevarr%C3%ADa" class="mw-redirect" title="José Antonio Echevarría">José Antonio Echevarría</a> (1932–1957).<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> However, the best known of these anti-Batista groups was the "<a href="/wiki/26th_of_July_Movement" title="26th of July Movement">26th of July Movement</a>" (MR-26-7), founded by a lawyer named <a href="/wiki/Fidel_Castro" title="Fidel Castro">Fidel Castro</a>. With Castro as the MR-26-7's head, the organization was based upon a <a href="/wiki/Clandestine_cell_system" title="Clandestine cell system">clandestine cell system</a>, with each cell containing ten members, none of whom knew the whereabouts or activities of the other cells.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Between December 1956 and 1959, Castro led a <a href="/wiki/Guerrilla" class="mw-redirect" title="Guerrilla">guerrilla</a> army against the forces of Batista from his base camp in the <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Maestra" title="Sierra Maestra">Sierra Maestra</a> mountains. Batista's repression of revolutionaries had earned him widespread unpopularity, and by 1958 his armies were in retreat. On 31 December 1958, Batista resigned and fled into exile, taking with him an amassed fortune of more than <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">US$</a>300,000,000.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Coltman_2003._p._137_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Coltman_2003._p._137-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> The presidency fell to Castro's chosen candidate, the lawyer <a href="/wiki/Manuel_Urrutia_Lle%C3%B3" title="Manuel Urrutia Lleó">Manuel Urrutia Lleó</a>, while members of the MR-26-7 took control of most positions in the cabinet.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> On 16 February 1959, Castro himself took on the role of Prime Minister.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Dismissing the need for elections, Castro proclaimed the new administration an example of <a href="/wiki/Direct_democracy" title="Direct democracy">direct democracy</a>, in which the Cuban populace could assemble <i>en masse</i> at demonstrations and express their democratic will to him personally.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> Critics instead condemned the new regime as un-democratic.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_counter-revolution">The counter-revolution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bay_of_Pigs_Invasion&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: The counter-revolution">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:CheyFidel.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/CheyFidel.jpg/220px-CheyFidel.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="294" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/CheyFidel.jpg/330px-CheyFidel.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/CheyFidel.jpg/440px-CheyFidel.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1197" data-file-height="1600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:CheyFidel.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Che_Guevara" title="Che Guevara">Che Guevara</a> (left) and <a href="/wiki/Fidel_Castro" title="Fidel Castro">Castro</a>, photographed by <a href="/wiki/Alberto_Korda" title="Alberto Korda">Alberto Korda</a> in 1961.</div></div></div>
<p>Soon after the success of the Cuban Revolution, militant counter-revolutionary groups developed in an attempt to overthrow the new regime. Undertaking armed attacks against government forces, some set up guerrilla bases in Cuba's mountainous regions, leading to the six-year <a href="/wiki/Escambray_Rebellion" class="mw-redirect" title="Escambray Rebellion">Escambray Rebellion</a>. These dissidents were funded and armed by various foreign sources, including the exiled Cuban community, the US <a href="/wiki/Central_Intelligence_Agency" title="Central Intelligence Agency">Central Intelligence Agency</a> (CIA), and <a href="/wiki/Rafael_Trujillo" title="Rafael Trujillo">Rafael Trujillo</a>'s regime in the <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican Republic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ros_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ros-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/No_quarter" title="No quarter">No quarter</a> was given during the suppression of the resistance in the <a href="/wiki/Escambray_Mountains" title="Escambray Mountains">Escambray Mountains</a>, where former rebels from the war against Batista took different sides.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> On 3 April 1961, a bomb attack on militia barracks in <a href="/wiki/Bayamo" title="Bayamo">Bayamo</a> killed four militia, and wounded eight more. On 6 April, the Hershey Sugar factory in Matanzas was destroyed by sabotage.<sup id="cite_ref-corzo_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-corzo-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> On 14 April 1961, guerrillas led by Agapito Rivera fought Cuban government forces near Las Cruces, Montembo, Las Villas, where several government troops were killed and others wounded.<sup id="cite_ref-corzo_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-corzo-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> Also on 14 April 1961, a <a href="/wiki/Cubana_de_Aviaci%C3%B3n_S.A." class="mw-redirect" title="Cubana de Aviación S.A.">Cubana</a> airliner was hijacked and flown to <a href="/wiki/Jacksonville,_Florida" title="Jacksonville, Florida">Jacksonville, Florida</a>; resultant confusion then helped the staged 'defection' of a B-26 and pilot at Miami on 15 April.<sup id="cite_ref-fernandez_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fernandez-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Castro's government began a crackdown on this opposition movement, arresting hundreds of dissidents.<sup id="cite_ref-Bourne_1986._p._197_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bourne_1986._p._197-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> Though it rejected the physical torture Batista's regime had used, Castro's government-sanctioned psychological torture, subjecting some prisoners to solitary confinement, rough treatment, hunger, and threatening behavior.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> After conservative editors and journalists began expressing hostility towards the government following its left-ward turn, the pro-Castro printers' trade union began to harass and disrupt editorial staff actions. In January 1960, the government proclaimed that each newspaper was obliged to publish a "clarification" by the printers' union at the end of every article that criticized the government. These "clarifications" signaled the start of press censorship in Castro's Cuba.<sup id="cite_ref-Bourne_1986._p._197_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bourne_1986._p._197-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Popular uproar across Cuba demanded that those figures who had been complicit in the widespread torture and killing of civilians be brought to justice. Although he remained a moderating force and tried to prevent the mass reprisal killings of Batistanos advocated by many Cubans, Castro helped to set up trials of many figures involved in the old regime across the country, resulting in hundreds of executions. Critics, in particular from the U.S. press, argued that many of these did not meet the standards of a <a href="/wiki/Fair_trial" class="mw-redirect" title="Fair trial">fair trial</a>, and condemned Cuba's new government as being more interested in vengeance than justice. Castro retaliated strongly against such accusations, proclaiming that "revolutionary justice is not based on legal precepts, but on moral conviction." In a show of support for this "revolutionary justice," he organized the first <a href="/wiki/Havana" title="Havana">Havana</a> trial to take place before a mass audience of 17,000 at the <a href="/wiki/Estadio_Latinoamericano" title="Estadio Latinoamericano">Sports Palace stadium</a>. When a group of aviators accused of bombing a village was found not guilty, he ordered a retrial, in which they were instead found guilty and sentenced to life imprisonment.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> On 11 March 1961, Jesus Carreras and American <a href="/wiki/William_Alexander_Morgan" title="William Alexander Morgan">William Alexander Morgan</a> (a former Castro ally) were executed after a trial.<sup id="cite_ref-thomas_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thomas-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nsa_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nsa-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tensions_with_the_United_States">Tensions with the United States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bay_of_Pigs_Invasion&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Tensions with the United States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Castro's Cuban government ordered the country's oil refineries – then controlled by US corporations <a href="/wiki/Esso" title="Esso">Esso</a> and <a href="/wiki/Standard_Oil" title="Standard Oil">Standard Oil</a> and Anglo-Dutch <a href="/wiki/Shell_Oil_Company" title="Shell Oil Company">Shell</a> – to process crude oil purchased from the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>, but under pressure from the US government, these companies refused. Castro responded by expropriating the refineries and <a href="/wiki/Nationalization" title="Nationalization">nationalizing</a> them under state control. In retaliation, the US canceled its import of Cuban sugar, provoking Castro to nationalize most US-owned assets, including banks and sugar mills.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> Relations between Cuba and the US were further strained following the explosion and sinking of a French vessel, the <i><a href="/wiki/Le_Coubre" class="mw-redirect" title="Le Coubre">Le Coubre</a></i>, in Havana harbor in March 1960. The cause of the explosion was never determined, but Castro publicly mentioned that the US government were guilty of sabotage.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> On 13 October 1960, the US government then prohibited the majority of exports to Cuba – the exceptions being medicines and certain foodstuffs – marking the start of <a href="/wiki/United_States_embargo_against_Cuba" title="United States embargo against Cuba">an economic embargo</a>. In retaliation, the Cuban National Institute for Agrarian Reform took control of 383 private-run businesses on 14 October, and on 25 October a further 166 US companies operating in Cuba had their premises seized and nationalized, including <a href="/wiki/Coca-Cola" title="Coca-Cola">Coca-Cola</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sears_Roebuck" class="mw-redirect" title="Sears Roebuck">Sears Roebuck</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Bourne_1986._p._214_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bourne_1986._p._214-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> On 16 December, the US then ended its <a href="/wiki/Import_quota" title="Import quota">import quota</a> of Cuban sugar.<sup id="cite_ref-Bourne_1986._p._215_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bourne_1986._p._215-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The US government was becoming increasingly critical of Castro's revolutionary government. At an August 1960 meeting of the <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_American_States" title="Organization of American States">Organization of American States</a> (OAS) held in <a href="/wiki/Costa_Rica" title="Costa Rica">Costa Rica</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_State" title="United States Secretary of State">US Secretary of State</a>, <a href="/wiki/Christian_Herter" title="Christian Herter">Christian Herter</a>, publicly proclaimed that Castro's administration was "following faithfully the <a href="/wiki/Bolshevik_Party" class="mw-redirect" title="Bolshevik Party">Bolshevik</a> pattern" by instituting a single-party political system, taking governmental control of <a href="/wiki/Trade_union" title="Trade union">trade unions</a>, suppressing <a href="/wiki/Civil_liberties" title="Civil liberties">civil liberties</a>, and removing both the <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_speech" title="Freedom of speech">freedom of speech</a> and <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_the_press" title="Freedom of the press">freedom of the press</a>. He furthermore asserted that <a href="/wiki/International_communism" class="mw-redirect" title="International communism">international communism</a> was using Cuba as an "operational base" for spreading revolution in the western hemisphere, and called on other OAS members to condemn the Cuban government for its breach of <a href="/wiki/Human_rights" title="Human rights">human rights</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> In turn, Castro lambasted the treatment of black people and the working classes he had witnessed in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York</a>, which he ridiculed as that "superfree, superdemocratic, superhumane, and supercivilized city." Proclaiming that the US poor were living "in the bowels of the imperialist monster," he attacked the mainstream US media and accused it of being controlled by big business.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> It must be noted that, on the surface, the US was trying to improve its relationship with <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>. Several negotiations between representatives from Cuba and the US took place around this time. Repairing international financial relations was the focal point of these discussions.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> Political relations were another hot topic of these conferences. The US stated that they would not interfere with Cuba's choice of government or its domestic structure; however, the US also ordered the Cubans to sever all ties with the Soviet Union.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In August 1960, the <a href="/wiki/CIA" class="mw-redirect" title="CIA">CIA</a> contacted the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Outfit" title="Chicago Outfit">Cosa Nostra in Chicago</a> with the intention to draft a simultaneous assassination of Fidel Castro, <a href="/wiki/Ra%C3%BAl_Castro" title="Raúl Castro">Raúl Castro</a> and Che Guevara. In exchange, if the operation were a success and a pro-US government were restored in Cuba, the CIA agreed that the <a href="/wiki/American_Mafia" title="American Mafia">Mafia</a> would get their "monopoly on gaming, prostitution and drugs."<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Tensions percolated when the CIA began to act on its desires to snuff out Castro. The general public became aware of the attempts to assassinate Castro in 1975 when a report entitled "Alleged Assassination Plots Involving Foreign Leaders" was released by the Senate <a href="/wiki/Church_Committee" title="Church Committee">Church Committee</a> set up to investigate CIA abuses.<sup id="cite_ref-Castro_Assassination_Plots_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Castro_Assassination_Plots-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> Efforts to murder Castro officially commenced in 1960.<sup id="cite_ref-Castro_Assassination_Plots_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Castro_Assassination_Plots-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> Some methods that the CIA undertook to murder Castro were creative, for example: "poison pills, an exploding sea shell, and a planned gift of a diving suit contaminated with toxins."<sup id="cite_ref-Castro_Assassination_Plots_66-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Castro_Assassination_Plots-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> More traditional ways of assassinating Castro were also planned, such as elimination via high-powered rifles with telescopic sights.<sup id="cite_ref-Castro_Assassination_Plots_66-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Castro_Assassination_Plots-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> In 1963, at the same time the Kennedy administration initiated secret peace overtures to Castro, the Cuban revolutionary and undercover CIA agent, <a href="/wiki/Rolando_Cubela_Secades" title="Rolando Cubela Secades">Rolando Cubela</a>, was tasked with killing Castro by the CIA official, <a href="/wiki/Desmond_Fitzgerald_(CIA_officer)" title="Desmond Fitzgerald (CIA officer)">Desmond Fitzgerald</a>, who portrayed himself as a personal representative of Robert Kennedy.<sup id="cite_ref-Castro_Assassination_Plots_66-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Castro_Assassination_Plots-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Preparation">Preparation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bay_of_Pigs_Invasion&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Preparation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_plans">Early plans</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bay_of_Pigs_Invasion&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Early plans">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The idea of overthrowing Castro's dictatorship first emerged within the <a href="/wiki/Central_Intelligence_Agency" title="Central Intelligence Agency">Central Intelligence Agency</a> (CIA), an independent civilian intelligence agency of the United States government, in early 1960. Founded in 1947 by the <a href="/wiki/National_Security_Act_of_1947" title="National Security Act of 1947">National Security Act</a>, the CIA was "a product of the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>", having been designed to counter the espionage activities of the Soviet Union's own national security agency, the <a href="/wiki/KGB" title="KGB">KGB</a>. As the perceived threat of <a href="/wiki/International_communism" class="mw-redirect" title="International communism">international communism</a> grew larger, the CIA expanded its activities to undertake covert economic, political, and military activities that would advance causes favourable to U.S. interests, often resulting in brutal dictatorships that favored US interests.<sup id="cite_ref-Quirk_1993._p._303_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Quirk_1993._p._303-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Director_of_Central_Intelligence" title="Director of Central Intelligence">CIA's Director</a> at the time, <a href="/wiki/Allen_Dulles" title="Allen Dulles">Allen Dulles</a>, was responsible for overseeing covert operations across the world, and although widely considered an ineffectual administrator, he was immensely popular among his employees, whom he had protected from the accusations of <a href="/wiki/McCarthyism" title="McCarthyism">McCarthyism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> Recognizing that Castro and his government were becoming increasingly hostile and openly opposed to the United States, President Dwight D. Eisenhower directed the Central Intelligence Agency to begin preparations of invading Cuba and overthrowing the Castro regime.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> The man overseeing plans for the Bay of Pigs Invasion was <a href="/wiki/Richard_M._Bissell_Jr." title="Richard M. Bissell Jr.">Richard M. Bissell Jr.</a>, the CIA's <a href="/wiki/Deputy_Director_for_Plans" class="mw-redirect" title="Deputy Director for Plans">Deputy Director for Plans</a> (DDP). He assembled a number of other agents to aid him in the plot, many of whom had worked on the <a href="/wiki/1954_Guatemalan_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="1954 Guatemalan coup d&#39;état">1954 Guatemalan coup</a> six years before; these included <a href="/wiki/David_Atlee_Phillips" title="David Atlee Phillips">David Philips</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gerry_Droller" title="Gerry Droller">Gerry Droller</a> and <a href="/wiki/E._Howard_Hunt" title="E. Howard Hunt">E. Howard Hunt</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Bissell placed Droller in charge of liaising with anti-Castro segments of the <a href="/wiki/Cuban-American" class="mw-redirect" title="Cuban-American">Cuban-American</a> community living in the United States, and asked Hunt to fashion a <a href="/wiki/Government-in-exile" class="mw-redirect" title="Government-in-exile">government-in-exile</a>, which the CIA would effectively control.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> Hunt proceeded to travel to <a href="/wiki/Havana" title="Havana">Havana</a>, the capital city of Cuba, where he spoke with Cubans from various backgrounds and discovered a <a href="/wiki/Brothel" title="Brothel">brothel</a> through the <a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz" title="Mercedes-Benz">Mercedes-Benz</a> agency.<sup id="cite_ref-Quirk_1993._p._308_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Quirk_1993._p._308-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> Returning to the US, he informed the Cuban-Americans with whom he was liaising that they would have to move their base of operations from <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a> to <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City" title="Mexico City">Mexico City</a>, because the <a href="/wiki/State_Department" class="mw-redirect" title="State Department">State Department</a> refused to permit the training of a militia on US soil. Although unhappy with the news, they conceded to the order.<sup id="cite_ref-Quirk_1993._p._308_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Quirk_1993._p._308-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>President had meetings with Kennedy at the White House on 6 December 1960, and 19 January 1961.<sup id="cite_ref-kennedyinvasion_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kennedyinvasion-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> In one conversation, Eisenhower stated that since March 1960, the US government had training "in small units, but we had done nothing else": "some hundreds of refugees" in Guatemala, "a few in Panama, and some in Florida."<sup id="cite_ref-kennedyinvasion_73-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kennedyinvasion-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> However, Eisenhower also expressed disapproval of the idea of Batista returning to power and was waiting for the exiles to agree on a leader who was opposed to both Castro and Batista.<sup id="cite_ref-kennedyinvasion_73-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kennedyinvasion-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Eisenhower.27s_approval"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Eisenhower's_approval">Eisenhower's approval</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bay_of_Pigs_Invasion&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Eisenhower&#039;s approval">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dwight_D._Eisenhower,_official_photo_portrait,_May_29,_1959.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Dwight_D._Eisenhower%2C_official_photo_portrait%2C_May_29%2C_1959.jpg/220px-Dwight_D._Eisenhower%2C_official_photo_portrait%2C_May_29%2C_1959.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="276" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Dwight_D._Eisenhower%2C_official_photo_portrait%2C_May_29%2C_1959.jpg/330px-Dwight_D._Eisenhower%2C_official_photo_portrait%2C_May_29%2C_1959.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Dwight_D._Eisenhower%2C_official_photo_portrait%2C_May_29%2C_1959.jpg/440px-Dwight_D._Eisenhower%2C_official_photo_portrait%2C_May_29%2C_1959.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2782" data-file-height="3484" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dwight_D._Eisenhower,_official_photo_portrait,_May_29,_1959.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>President <a href="/wiki/Dwight_D._Eisenhower" title="Dwight D. Eisenhower">Dwight D. Eisenhower</a>, who authorized the <a href="/wiki/Central_Intelligence_Agency" title="Central Intelligence Agency">Central Intelligence Agency</a> to plan the Bay of Pigs Invasion</div></div></div>
<p>On 17 March 1960, the CIA put forward their plan for the overthrow of Castro's administration to the <a href="/wiki/U.S._National_Security_Council" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. National Security Council">U.S. National Security Council</a> (NSC) where US President <a href="/wiki/Dwight_D._Eisenhower" title="Dwight D. Eisenhower">Dwight D. Eisenhower</a> lended his support.<sup id="cite_ref-Quirk_1993._p._303_67-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Quirk_1993._p._303-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> The first stated objective of the plan was to "bring about the replacement of the Castro regime with one more devoted to the true interests of the Cuban people and more acceptable to the US in such a manner to avoid any appearance of US intervention."<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> Four major forms of action were to be taken to aid anti-communist opposition in Cuba at the time.  These included providing a powerful propaganda offensive against the regime, perfect a covert intelligence network within Cuba, developing paramilitary forces outside of Cuba, and acquiring the necessary logistical support for covert military operations on the island. At this stage, however, it was still not clear that an invasion would take place.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> Contrary to popular belief, however, documents obtained from Eisenhower Library revealed that Eisenhower never ordered, or approved plans, for an amphibious assault on Cuba.<sup id="cite_ref-kennedyinvasion_73-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kennedyinvasion-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 18 August 1960, Eisenhower approved a budget of $13,000,000 for the operation. By 31 October 1960, most guerrilla infiltrations and supply drops directed by the CIA into Cuba had failed, and developments of further guerrilla strategies were replaced by plans to mount an initial amphibious assault, with a minimum of 1,500 men. The election of John Kennedy as US President sped up preparations for the invasion;<sup id="cite_ref-kennedyinvasion_73-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kennedyinvasion-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> Kennedy reached out to Cuban exiles who supported Batista and hinted he was willing to bring Batista back to power in order to overthrow Castro.<sup id="cite_ref-batistaattempt_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-batistaattempt-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> On 18 November 1960, <a href="/wiki/Allen_Dulles" title="Allen Dulles">Allen Dulles</a> and <a href="/wiki/Richard_M._Bissell,_Jr." class="mw-redirect" title="Richard M. Bissell, Jr.">Richard Bissell</a> first briefed President-elect John Kennedy on the outline plans. Having experience in actions such as the <a href="/wiki/1954_Guatemalan_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="1954 Guatemalan coup d&#39;état">1954 Guatemalan coup d'état</a>, Dulles was confident that the CIA was capable of overthrowing the Cuban government. On 29 November 1960, President Eisenhower met with the chiefs of the CIA, Defense, State, and Treasury departments to discuss the new concept. None expressed any objections, and Eisenhower approved the plans with the intention of persuading John Kennedy of their merit. On 8 December 1960, Bissell presented outline plans to the "<a href="/wiki/Oversight_of_United_States_covert_operations" title="Oversight of United States covert operations">Special Group</a>" while declining to commit details to written records. Further development of the plans continued, and on 4 January 1961 they consisted of an intention to establish a "lodgement" by 750 men at an undisclosed site in Cuba, supported by considerable air power.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGleijeses19959–19_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGleijeses19959–19-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Meanwhile, in the <a href="/wiki/1960_United_States_presidential_election" title="1960 United States presidential election">1960 presidential election</a>, both main candidates, <a href="/wiki/Richard_Nixon" title="Richard Nixon">Richard Nixon</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republican Party</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy" title="John F. Kennedy">John F. Kennedy</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democratic Party</a>, campaigned on the issue of Cuba, with both candidates taking a hardline stance on Castro.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> Nixon – who was then Vice President – insisted that Kennedy should not be informed of the military plans, to which Dulles conceded.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> To Nixon's chagrin, the Kennedy campaign released a scathing statement on the Eisenhower administration's Cuba policy on 20 October 1960 which said that "we must attempt to strengthen the non-Batista democratic anti-Castro forces [...] who offer eventual hope of overthrowing Castro", claiming that "Thus far these fighters for freedom have had virtually no support from our Government."<sup id="cite_ref-batistaattempt_76-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-batistaattempt-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> At the last election debate the next day, Nixon called Kennedy's proposed course of action "dangerously irresponsible" and even lectured Kennedy on international law,<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> in effect denigrating the policy Nixon himself favored.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Kennedy.27s_operational_approval"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Kennedy's_operational_approval">Kennedy's operational approval</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bay_of_Pigs_Invasion&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Kennedy&#039;s operational approval">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><div class="mediaContainer" style="width:220px"><audio id="mwe_player_0" controls="" preload="none" style="width:220px" class="kskin" data-durationhint="347.78848072562" data-startoffset="0" data-mwtitle="Kennedy_on_Cuba_12_April_1961.ogg" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons"><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/0/0f/Kennedy_on_Cuba_12_April_1961.ogg/Kennedy_on_Cuba_12_April_1961.ogg.mp3" type="audio/mpeg" data-title="MP3" data-shorttitle="MP3" data-transcodekey="mp3" data-width="0" data-height="0" data-bandwidth="109304" /><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/0f/Kennedy_on_Cuba_12_April_1961.ogg" type="audio/ogg; codecs=&quot;vorbis&quot;" data-title="Original Ogg file (120 kbps)" data-shorttitle="Ogg source" data-width="0" data-height="0" data-bandwidth="119979" /></audio></div>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kennedy_on_Cuba_12_April_1961.ogg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy" title="John F. Kennedy">John F. Kennedy</a> answered difficult questions on Cuba on 12 April, only five days before the invasion</div></div></div>
<p>On 28 January 1961, President Kennedy was briefed, together with all the major departments, on the latest plan (code-named <i>Operation Pluto</i>), which involved 1,000 men landed in a ship-borne invasion at <a href="/wiki/Trinidad,_Cuba" title="Trinidad, Cuba">Trinidad</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>, about 270&#160;km (170&#160;mi) south-east of <a href="/wiki/Havana" title="Havana">Havana</a>, at the foothills of the <a href="/wiki/Escambray_Mountains" title="Escambray Mountains">Escambray Mountains</a> in <a href="/wiki/Sancti_Spiritus" class="mw-redirect" title="Sancti Spiritus">Sancti Spiritus</a> province. Kennedy authorized the active departments to continue, and to report progress.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGleijeses199520_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGleijeses199520-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> Trinidad had good port facilities, it was closer to many existing counter-revolutionary activities, and it offered an escape route into the Escambray Mountains. That scheme was subsequently rejected by the State Department because the airfield there was not large enough for B-26 bombers and, since B-26s were to play a prominent role in the invasion, this would destroy the façade that the invasion was just an uprising with no American involvement. <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_State" title="United States Secretary of State">Secretary of State</a> <a href="/wiki/Dean_Rusk" title="Dean Rusk">Dean Rusk</a> raised some eyebrows by contemplating airdropping a bulldozer to extend the airfield.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> Kennedy rejected Trinidad, preferring a more low-key locale.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuesada200916_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuesada200916-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> On 4 April 1961, President Kennedy then approved the Bay of Pigs plan (also known as <i>Operation Zapata</i>), because it had a sufficiently long airfield, it was farther away from large groups of civilians than the <a href="/wiki/Trinidad" title="Trinidad">Trinidad</a> plan, and it was less "noisy" militarily, which would make denial of direct US involvement more plausible.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuesada200917_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuesada200917-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> The invasion landing area was changed to beaches bordering the Bahía de Cochinos (Bay of Pigs) in <a href="/wiki/Las_Villas_Province" class="mw-redirect" title="Las Villas Province">Las Villas Province</a>, 150&#160;km southeast of Havana, and east of the <a href="/wiki/Zapata_Peninsula" title="Zapata Peninsula">Zapata Peninsula</a>. The landings were to take place at Playa Girón (code-named <i>Blue Beach</i>), Playa Larga (code-named <i>Red Beach</i>), and Caleta Buena Inlet (code-named <i>Green Beach</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-jones_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jones-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-higgins_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-higgins-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-faria_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-faria-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-kornbluh_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kornbluh-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Top aides to Kennedy, such as Dean Rusk and both Joint Chiefs of staff, later said that they had hesitations about the plans but muted their thoughts. Some leaders blamed these problems on the "Cold War mindset" or the determination of the Kennedy brothers to oust Castro and fulfill campaign promises.<sup id="cite_ref-jones_86-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jones-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> Military advisers were skeptical of its potential for success as well.<sup id="cite_ref-kennedyinvasion_73-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kennedyinvasion-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> Despite these hesitations, Kennedy still ordered the attack to take place.<sup id="cite_ref-kennedyinvasion_73-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kennedyinvasion-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In March 1961, the CIA helped Cuban exiles in Miami to create the <a href="/wiki/Cuban_Revolutionary_Council" title="Cuban Revolutionary Council">Cuban Revolutionary Council</a> (CRC), chaired by <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mir%C3%B3_Cardona" title="José Miró Cardona">José Miró Cardona</a>, former Prime Minister of Cuba in January 1959. Cardona became the de facto leader-in-waiting of the intended post-invasion Cuban government.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Training">Training</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bay_of_Pigs_Invasion&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Training">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BayofPigsPrep2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/BayofPigsPrep2.jpg/220px-BayofPigsPrep2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="176" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/BayofPigsPrep2.jpg/330px-BayofPigsPrep2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/BayofPigsPrep2.jpg/440px-BayofPigsPrep2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="774" data-file-height="619" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BayofPigsPrep2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Douglas_A-26_Invader" title="Douglas A-26 Invader">Douglas A-26 Invader</a> "B-26" bomber aircraft disguised as a Cuban model</div></div></div>
<p>In April 1960, the CIA began to recruit anti-Castro Cuban exiles in the <a href="/wiki/Miami" title="Miami">Miami</a> area. Until July 1960, assessment and training was carried out on <a href="/wiki/Useppa_Island" title="Useppa Island">Useppa Island</a> and at various other facilities in South Florida, such as <a href="/wiki/Homestead_AFB" class="mw-redirect" title="Homestead AFB">Homestead AFB</a>. Specialist guerrilla training took place at <a href="/wiki/Fort_Gulick" title="Fort Gulick">Fort Gulick</a>, <a href="/wiki/Panama" title="Panama">Panama</a> and at <a href="/wiki/Fort_Clayton" title="Fort Clayton">Fort Clayton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Panama" title="Panama">Panama</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-fernandez_40-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fernandez-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERodríguez199978_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERodríguez199978-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> The force that became <a href="/wiki/Brigade_2506" title="Brigade 2506">Brigade 2506</a> started with 28 men, who initially were told that their training was being paid for by an anonymous Cuban millionaire émigré, but the recruits soon guessed who was paying the bills, calling their supposed anonymous benefactor "Uncle Sam", and the pretense was dropped.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuesada200910_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuesada200910-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> The overall leader was Dr. <a href="/wiki/Manuel_Artime" title="Manuel Artime">Manuel Artime</a> while the military leader was <a href="/wiki/Pepe_San_Rom%C3%A1n" title="Pepe San Román">José "Pepe" Peréz San Román</a>, a former Cuban Army officer imprisoned under both Batista and Castro.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuesada200910_92-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuesada200910-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BayofPigsPrep3.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/BayofPigsPrep3.jpg/220px-BayofPigsPrep3.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/BayofPigsPrep3.jpg/330px-BayofPigsPrep3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/BayofPigsPrep3.jpg/440px-BayofPigsPrep3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="775" data-file-height="580" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BayofPigsPrep3.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Cuban defectors practicing parachute drops</div></div></div>
<p>For the increasing ranks of recruits, infantry training was carried out at a CIA-run base (code-named <i>JMTrax</i>) near <a href="/wiki/Retalhuleu" title="Retalhuleu">Retalhuleu</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Madre_de_Chiapas" title="Sierra Madre de Chiapas">Sierra Madre</a> on the Pacific coast of Guatemala.<sup id="cite_ref-johnson_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-johnson-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> The exiled group named themselves <a href="/wiki/Brigade_2506" title="Brigade 2506">Brigade 2506</a> (<i>Brigada Asalto 2506</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-johnson_93-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-johnson-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> In summer 1960, an airfield (code-named <i>JMadd</i>, aka <i>Rayo Base</i>) was constructed near Retalhuleu, Guatemala. Gunnery and flight training of Brigade 2506 aircrews was carried out by personnel from <a href="/wiki/Alabama_Air_National_Guard" title="Alabama Air National Guard">Alabama ANG</a> (Air National Guard) under General Reid Doster, using at least six Douglas <a href="/wiki/B-26_Invader" class="mw-redirect" title="B-26 Invader">B-26 Invaders</a> in the markings of <a href="/wiki/Fuerza_A%C3%A9rea_Guatemalteca" class="mw-redirect" title="Fuerza Aérea Guatemalteca">Fuerza Aérea Guatemalteca</a>, legitimate delivery of those being delayed by about six months.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuesada200911–12_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuesada200911–12-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> An additional 26 B-26s were obtained from US military stocks, 'sanitized' at <a href="/wiki/Duke_Field" title="Duke Field">'Field Three'</a> to obscure their origins, and about 20 of them were converted for offensive operations by removal of defensive armament, standardization of the 'eight-gun nose', addition of underwing drop tanks and rocket racks.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-hagedorn2006_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hagedorn2006-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> Paratroop training was at a base nicknamed <i>Garrapatenango</i>, near <a href="/wiki/Quetzaltenango" title="Quetzaltenango">Quetzaltenango</a>, Guatemala. Training for boat handling and amphibious landings took place at <a href="/wiki/Vieques" class="mw-redirect" title="Vieques">Vieques</a> Island, Puerto Rico. Tank training for the Brigade 2506 <a href="/wiki/M41_Walker_Bulldog" title="M41 Walker Bulldog">M41 Walker Bulldog</a> tanks,<sup id="cite_ref-weaponsandwarfare.com_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-weaponsandwarfare.com-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> took place at <a href="/wiki/Fort_Knox" title="Fort Knox">Fort Knox</a>, Kentucky, and <a href="/wiki/Fort_Benning" title="Fort Benning">Fort Benning</a>, Georgia. Underwater demolition and infiltration training took place at <a href="/wiki/Belle_Chase" class="mw-redirect" title="Belle Chase">Belle Chase</a> near New Orleans.<sup id="cite_ref-kornbluh_89-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kornbluh-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> To create a navy, the CIA purchased five cargo ships from the Cuban-owned, but Miami-based Garcia Line, thereby giving "plausible deniability" as the <a href="/wiki/State_Department" class="mw-redirect" title="State Department">State Department</a> had insisted no US ships could be involved in the invasion.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuesada200913_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuesada200913-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> The first four of the five ships, namely the <i>Atlantico</i>, the <i>Caribe</i>, the <i>Houston</i> and <i>Río Escondido</i> were to carry enough supplies and weapons to last thirty days while the <i>Lake Charles</i> had 15 days of supplies and was intended to land the provisional government of Cuba.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuesada200913_98-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuesada200913-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> The ships were loaded with supplies at New Orleans and sailed to <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Cabezas" title="Puerto Cabezas">Puerto Cabezas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nicaragua" title="Nicaragua">Nicaragua</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuesada200913_98-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuesada200913-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> Additionally, the invasion force had two old Landing Craft Infantry (LCI) ships, the <i>Blagar</i> and <i>Barbara J</i> from World War II that were part of the CIA's "ghost ship" fleet and served as command ships for the invasion.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuesada200913_98-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuesada200913-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> The crews of the supply ships were Cuban while the crews of the LCIs were Americans, borrowed by the CIA from the Military Sea Transportation Service (MSTS)<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuesada200913_98-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuesada200913-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> One CIA officer wrote that MSTS sailors were all professional and experienced, but not trained for combat.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuesada200913_98-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuesada200913-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In November 1960, the Retalhuleu recruits took part in quelling an officers' rebellion in Guatemala, in addition to the intervention of the US Navy.<sup id="cite_ref-revolutionaries_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-revolutionaries-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The CIA transported people, supplies, and arms from Florida to all the bases at night, using <a href="/wiki/Douglas_C-54" class="mw-redirect" title="Douglas C-54">Douglas C-54</a> transports. On 9 April 1961, Brigade 2506 personnel, ships, and aircraft started transferring from <a href="/wiki/Guatemala" title="Guatemala">Guatemala</a> to Puerto Cabezas.<sup id="cite_ref-nsa_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nsa-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Curtiss_C-46" class="mw-redirect" title="Curtiss C-46">Curtiss C-46s</a> were also used for transport between Retalhuleu and a CIA base (code-named <i>JMTide</i>, aka <i>Happy Valley</i>) at Puerto Cabezas.
</p><p>Facilities and limited logistical assistance were provided by the governments of General <a href="/wiki/Miguel_Yd%C3%ADgoras_Fuentes" title="Miguel Ydígoras Fuentes">Miguel Ydígoras Fuentes</a> in Guatemala, and General <a href="/wiki/Luis_Somoza_Debayle" title="Luis Somoza Debayle">Luis Somoza Debayle</a> in Nicaragua, but no military personnel or equipment of those nations was directly employed in the conflict.<sup id="cite_ref-hagedorn2006_96-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hagedorn2006-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> Both governments later received military training and equipment, including some of the CIA's remaining B-26s.
</p><p>In early 1961, Cuba's army possessed <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet</a>-designed <a href="/wiki/T-34" title="T-34">T-34</a> medium tanks, <a href="/wiki/IS-2" class="mw-redirect" title="IS-2">IS-2</a> heavy tanks, <a href="/wiki/SU-100" title="SU-100">SU-100</a> <a href="/wiki/Tank_destroyers" class="mw-redirect" title="Tank destroyers">tank destroyers</a>, 122mm <a href="/wiki/Howitzer" title="Howitzer">howitzers</a>, other artillery and small arms plus <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italian</a> 105mm howitzers. The Cuban air force armed inventory included Douglas <a href="/wiki/B-26_Invader" class="mw-redirect" title="B-26 Invader">B-26 Invader</a> light bombers, <a href="/wiki/Hawker_Sea_Fury" title="Hawker Sea Fury">Hawker Sea Fury</a> fighters, and <a href="/wiki/T-33_Shooting_Star" class="mw-redirect" title="T-33 Shooting Star">Lockheed T-33</a> jets, all remaining from the <i>Fuerza Aérea del Ejército de Cuba</i> (FAEC), the Cuban air force of the <a href="/wiki/Fulgencio_Batista" title="Fulgencio Batista">Batista</a> government.<sup id="cite_ref-johnson_93-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-johnson-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Anticipating an invasion, <a href="/wiki/Che_Guevara" title="Che Guevara">Che Guevara</a> stressed the importance of an armed civilian populace, stating: "all of the Cuban people must become a <a href="/wiki/Guerrilla" class="mw-redirect" title="Guerrilla">guerrilla</a> army; each and every Cuban must learn to handle and if necessary use firearms in defense of the nation".<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Participants">Participants</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bay_of_Pigs_Invasion&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Participants">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="US_Government_personnel">US Government personnel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bay_of_Pigs_Invasion&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: US Government personnel">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In April 1960, FRD (<i>Frente Revolucionario Democratico</i> – Democratic Revolutionary Front) rebels were taken to <a href="/wiki/Useppa_Island" title="Useppa Island">Useppa Island</a>, a private island off the coast of Florida, which was covertly leased by the CIA at the time. Once the rebels had arrived, they were greeted by instructors from U.S. Army special forces groups, members from the U.S. Air Force and Air National Guard and members of the CIA. The rebels were trained in amphibious assault tactics, guerrilla warfare, infantry and weapons training, unit tactics and land navigation.
<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The recruiting of Cuban exiles in Miami was organized by CIA staff officers <a href="/wiki/E._Howard_Hunt" title="E. Howard Hunt">E. Howard Hunt</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gerry_Droller" title="Gerry Droller">Gerry Droller</a>. Detailed planning, training and military operations were conducted by <a href="/wiki/Jacob_Esterline" title="Jacob Esterline">Jacob Esterline</a>, Colonel <a href="/wiki/Jack_Hawkins_(US_Marine_Corps_officer)" class="mw-redirect" title="Jack Hawkins (US Marine Corps officer)">Jack Hawkins</a>, <a href="/wiki/F%C3%A9lix_Rodr%C3%ADguez_(soldier)" title="Félix Rodríguez (soldier)">Félix Rodríguez</a> and Colonel Stanley W. Beerli under the direction of Richard Bissell and his deputy <a href="/wiki/Tracy_Barnes" title="Tracy Barnes">Tracy Barnes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-kornbluh_89-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kornbluh-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuban_government_personnel">Cuban government personnel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bay_of_Pigs_Invasion&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Cuban government personnel">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Already, Fidel Castro was known as, and addressed as, the commander-in-chief of Cuban armed forces, with a nominal base at 'Point One' in Havana. In early April 1961, his brother <a href="/wiki/Ra%C3%BAl_Castro" title="Raúl Castro">Raúl Castro</a> was assigned command of forces in the east, based in <a href="/wiki/Santiago_de_Cuba" title="Santiago de Cuba">Santiago de Cuba</a>. <a href="/wiki/Che_Guevara" title="Che Guevara">Che Guevara</a> commanded western forces, based in <a href="/wiki/Pinar_del_R%C3%ADo" title="Pinar del Río">Pinar del Río</a>. Major <a href="/wiki/Juan_Almeida_Bosque" title="Juan Almeida Bosque">Juan Almeida Bosque</a> commanded forces in the central provinces, based in <a href="/wiki/Santa_Clara,_Cuba" title="Santa Clara, Cuba">Santa Clara</a>. Raúl Curbelo Morales was head of the air force. <a href="/wiki/Sergio_del_Valle_Jim%C3%A9nez" title="Sergio del Valle Jiménez">Sergio del Valle Jiménez</a> was Director of Headquarters Operations at Point One. <a href="/wiki/Efigenio_Ameijeiras" title="Efigenio Ameijeiras">Efigenio Ameijeiras</a> was the Head of the Revolutionary National Police. <a href="/wiki/Ramiro_Vald%C3%A9s" title="Ramiro Valdés">Ramiro Valdés Menéndez</a> was Minister of the Interior and head of G-2 (Seguridad del Estado, or state security). His deputy was Comandante <a href="/wiki/Manuel_Pi%C3%B1eiro" title="Manuel Piñeiro">Manuel Piñeiro Losada</a>, also known as 'Barba Roja'. Captain <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Ram%C3%B3n_Fern%C3%A1ndez" title="José Ramón Fernández">José Ramón Fernández</a> was head of the School of Militia Leaders (Cadets) at <a href="/wiki/Matanzas" title="Matanzas">Matanzas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-szulc1986_3-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-szulc1986-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERodríguez1999169_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERodríguez1999169-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-wyden_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wyden-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-kellnerp69_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kellnerp69-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Other commanders of units during the conflict included Major Raúl Menéndez Tomassevich, Major Filiberto Olivera Moya, Major René de los Santos, Major <a href="/wiki/Augusto_Mart%C3%ADnez_Sanchez" class="mw-redirect" title="Augusto Martínez Sanchez">Augusto Martínez Sanchez</a>, Major Félix Duque, Major Pedro Miret, Major Flavio Bravo, Major <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Luss%C3%B3n" class="mw-redirect" title="Antonio Lussón">Antonio Lussón</a>, Captain Orlando Pupo Pena, Captain <a href="/wiki/Victor_Dreke" class="mw-redirect" title="Victor Dreke">Victor Dreke</a>, Captain Emilio Aragonés, Captain Angel Fernández Vila, <a href="/wiki/Arnaldo_Ochoa" title="Arnaldo Ochoa">Arnaldo Ochoa</a>, and Orlando Rodriguez Puerta.<sup id="cite_ref-fernandez_40-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fernandez-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-dreke_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dreke-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Soviet-trained Spanish advisors were brought to Cuba from <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Bloc" title="Eastern Bloc">Eastern Bloc</a> countries. These advisors had held high staff positions in the Soviet armies during <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> and became known as "Hispano-Soviets," having long resided in the Soviet Union. The most senior of these was the Spanish communist veterans of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Civil_War" title="Spanish Civil War">Spanish Civil War</a>, <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Ciutat_de_Miguel" title="Francisco Ciutat de Miguel">Francisco Ciutat de Miguel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Enrique_L%C3%ADster" title="Enrique Líster">Enrique Líster</a>, and Cuban-born <a href="/wiki/Alberto_Bayo" title="Alberto Bayo">Alberto Bayo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> Ciutat de Miguel (Cuban alias: Ángel Martínez Riosola, commonly referred to as "Angelito"), was an advisor to forces in the central provinces. The role of other Soviet agents at the time is uncertain, but some of them acquired greater fame later. For example, two KGB colonels, Vadim Kochergin and Victor Simanov were first sighted in Cuba in about September 1959.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Prior_warnings_of_invasion">Prior warnings of invasion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bay_of_Pigs_Invasion&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Prior warnings of invasion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The Cuban security apparatus knew the invasion was coming, via their extensive secret intelligence network, as well as the loose talk by members of the brigade, some of which was heard in <a href="/wiki/Miami" title="Miami">Miami</a>, and was repeated in US and foreign newspaper reports. Nevertheless, days before the invasion, multiple acts of sabotage were carried out, such as the <a href="/wiki/El_Encanto_fire" title="El Encanto fire">El Encanto fire</a>, an arson attack in a department store in Havana on 13 April that killed one shop worker.<sup id="cite_ref-fernandez_40-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fernandez-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERodríguez1999123–25_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERodríguez1999123–25-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> The Cuban government also had been warned by senior <a href="/wiki/KGB" title="KGB">KGB</a> agents <a href="/w/index.php?title=Osvaldo_S%C3%A1nchez_Cabrera&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Osvaldo Sánchez Cabrera (page does not exist)">Osvaldo Sánchez Cabrera</a> and 'Aragon', who died violently before and after the invasion, respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> The general Cuban population was not well informed, except for CIA-funded <a href="/wiki/Pirate_radio_in_Central_America_and_Caribbean_Sea" class="mw-redirect" title="Pirate radio in Central America and Caribbean Sea">Radio Swan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> As of May 1960, almost all means of public communication were in the government's hands.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 29 April 2000, a <i><a href="/wiki/The_Washington_Post" title="The Washington Post">The Washington Post</a></i> article, "Soviets Knew Date of Cuba Attack", reported that the CIA had information indicating that the Soviet Union knew the invasion was going to take place, and did not inform Kennedy. On 13 April 1961, <a href="/wiki/Voice_of_Russia" title="Voice of Russia">Radio Moscow</a> broadcast an English-language newscast, predicting the invasion "in a plot hatched by the CIA" using paid "criminals" within a week. The invasion took place four days later.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/David_Ormsby-Gore" class="mw-redirect" title="David Ormsby-Gore">David Ormsby-Gore</a>, British Ambassador to the US, stated that British intelligence analysis, as made available to the CIA, indicated that the Cuban people were predominantly behind Castro, and that there was no likelihood of mass defections or insurrections.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Prelude_to_invasion">Prelude to invasion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bay_of_Pigs_Invasion&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Prelude to invasion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Acquisition_of_aircraft">Acquisition of aircraft</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bay_of_Pigs_Invasion&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Acquisition of aircraft">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>From June to September 1960, the most time consuming task was the acquisition of the aircraft to be used in the invasion.  The anti-Castro effort depended on the success of these aircraft.  Although models such as the C-46 and C-54 were to be used for airdrops and bomb drops as well as infiltration and exfiltration, they were looking for an aircraft that could perform tactical strikes.  The two models that were going to be decided on were the Navy's AD-5 Skyraider or the Air Force's light bomber, the B-26.  The AD-5 was readily available and ready for the Navy to train pilots, and in a meeting among a special group in the office of the Deputy Director of the CIA, the AD-5 was approved and decided on.  After a cost benefit analysis, word was sent that the AD-5 plan would be abandoned and the B-26 would take its place.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Fleet_sets_sail_.2814_April.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Fleet_sets_sail_(14_April)">Fleet sets sail (14 April)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bay_of_Pigs_Invasion&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Fleet sets sail (14 April)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Under cover of darkness, the invasion fleet set sail from <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Cabezas,_Nicaragua" class="mw-redirect" title="Puerto Cabezas, Nicaragua">Puerto Cabezas, Nicaragua</a> and headed towards the Bay of Pigs on the night of 14 April.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuesada200919_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuesada200919-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> After on-loading the attack planes in Norfolk Naval Base, and taking on prodigious quantities of food and supplies sufficient for the seven weeks at-sea to come, the crew knew from the hasty camouflage of the ship's and aircraft identifying numbers that a secret mission was on hand.  The Essex Group had been at sea for nearly a month before the invasion; its crew was well aware of the impending battle. On route, Essex had made a night time stop at a Navy arms depot in Charleston, SC to load tactical nuclear weapons to be held ready during the cruise. The afternoon of the invasion, one accompanying destroyer rendezvoused with Essex to have a gun mount repaired and put back into action; the ship displayed numerous shell casings on deck from its shore bombardment actions. On 16 April Essex was at General Quarters for most of a day; Soviet <a href="/wiki/MiG-15" class="mw-redirect" title="MiG-15">MiG-15s</a> made feints and close range fly overs that night, with Soviet Red Stars prominent.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Air_attacks_on_airfields_.2815_April.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Air_attacks_on_airfields_(15_April)">Air attacks on airfields (15 April)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bay_of_Pigs_Invasion&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Air attacks on airfields (15 April)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
