<p>Looking at both the <i>Survey of the Cuban Operation</i> and <i>Groupthink: Psychological Studies of Policy Decisions and Fiascoes</i> by <a href="/wiki/Irving_Janis" title="Irving Janis">Irving Janis</a>, it identifies the lack of communication and the mere assumption of concurrence to be the main causes behind the C.I.A and the president's collective failure to efficiently evaluate the facts before them. A considerable amount of information presented before President Kennedy proved to be false in reality, such as the support of the Cuban people for Fidel Castro, making it difficult to assess the actual situation and the future of the operation. The absence of the initiative to explore other options of the debate led the participants to remain optimistic and rigid in their belief that the mission would succeed, being unknowingly biased in the group psychology of <a href="/wiki/Wishful_thinking" title="Wishful thinking">wishful thinking</a> as well.
</p><p>In mid-1960, CIA operative <a href="/wiki/E._Howard_Hunt" title="E. Howard Hunt">E. Howard Hunt</a> had interviewed Cubans in Havana; in a 1997 interview with <a href="/wiki/CNN" title="CNN">CNN</a>, he said, "...all I could find was a lot of enthusiasm for Fidel Castro."<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Invasion_legacy_in_Cuba">Invasion legacy in Cuba</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bay_of_Pigs_Invasion&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Invasion legacy in Cuba">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Airplane_in_Museo_Giron.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Airplane_in_Museo_Giron.jpg/200px-Airplane_in_Museo_Giron.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="133" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Airplane_in_Museo_Giron.jpg/300px-Airplane_in_Museo_Giron.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Airplane_in_Museo_Giron.jpg/400px-Airplane_in_Museo_Giron.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1536" data-file-height="1020" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Airplane_in_Museo_Giron.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Sea Fury F 50 preserved at the Museo Giron, <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a> in 2006</div></div></div>
<p>For many Latin Americans, the Bay of Pigs Invasion served to reinforce the already widely held belief that the US could not be trusted. The invasion also illustrated that the US could be defeated, and thus, the failed invasion encouraged political groups across the Latin American region to find ways to undermine US influence.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Historians often attest the Bay of Pigs fiasco made Castro even more popular, adding nationalistic sentiments in support of his economic policies. Following the air attacks on Cuban airfields on 15 April, he declared the revolution "<a href="/wiki/Marxism-Leninism" class="mw-redirect" title="Marxism-Leninism">Marxist-Leninist</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-kellnerp69_105-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kellnerp69-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> After the invasion, he pursued closer relations with the Soviet Union, partly for protection, that helped pave the way for the 1962 <a href="/wiki/Cuban_Missile_Crisis" title="Cuban Missile Crisis">Cuban Missile Crisis</a>. Castro was then increasingly wary of further US intervention, and more open to Soviet suggestions of placing nuclear weapons on Cuba to ensure its security.
</p><p>In March 2001, shortly before the 40th anniversary of the invasion, a conference took place in Havana, attended by about 60 American delegates. The conference was titled Bay of Pigs: 40 Years After, co-sponsored by the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Havana" title="University of Havana">University of Havana</a> and the US-based <a href="/wiki/National_Security_Archive" title="National Security Archive">National Security Archive</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup> The conference was co-sponsored by <a href="/wiki/Universidad_de_La_Habana" class="mw-redirect" title="Universidad de La Habana">Universidad de La Habana</a> (University of Havana), Centro de Estudios Sobre Estados Unidos, <a href="/wiki/Instituto_de_Historia_de_Cuba" title="Instituto de Historia de Cuba">Instituto de Historia de Cuba</a>, Centro de Investigaciones Históricas de la Seguridad del Estado; Centro de Estudios Sobre America, and the US-based <a href="/wiki/National_Security_Archive" title="National Security Archive">National Security Archive</a>. It commenced on Thursday 22 March 2001 at the Hotel Palco, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Palacio_de_las_Convenciones&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Palacio de las Convenciones (page does not exist)">Palacio de las Convenciones</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&#160;&#91;<a href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palacio_de_las_Convenciones" class="extiw" title="es:Palacio de las Convenciones">es</a>&#93;</span>, La Habana.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup> On 24 March, following the formal conference, many of the delegates and observers travelled by road to Australia sugar mill, Playa Larga, and Playa Girón, the site of the initial landing in the invasion. A documentary film was made of that trip, titled <i>Cuba: The 40 Years War</i>, released on DVD in 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup> A Cuban FAR combatant at the Bay of Pigs, <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Ram%C3%B3n_Fern%C3%A1ndez" title="José Ramón Fernández">José Ramón Fernández</a>, attended the conference, as did four members of Brigade 2506, Roberto Carballo, Mario Cabello, Alfredo Duran, and Luis Tornes.
</p><p>There are still yearly nationwide drills in Cuba during the 'Dia de la Defensa' (Defense Day), to prepare the population for an invasion.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Invasion_legacy_for_Cuban_exiles">Invasion legacy for Cuban exiles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bay_of_Pigs_Invasion&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Invasion legacy for Cuban exiles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:LittleHavanOct06BayOfPigsMonument.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/LittleHavanOct06BayOfPigsMonument.jpg/200px-LittleHavanOct06BayOfPigsMonument.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="267" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/LittleHavanOct06BayOfPigsMonument.jpg/300px-LittleHavanOct06BayOfPigsMonument.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/LittleHavanOct06BayOfPigsMonument.jpg/400px-LittleHavanOct06BayOfPigsMonument.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2112" data-file-height="2816" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:LittleHavanOct06BayOfPigsMonument.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Bay of Pigs Memorial in <a href="/wiki/Little_Havana" title="Little Havana">Little Havana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Miami" title="Miami">Miami</a></div></div></div>
<p>Many who fought for the CIA in the conflict remained loyal after the event; some Bay of Pigs veterans became officers in the US Army in the <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_War" title="Vietnam War">Vietnam War</a>, including 6 colonels, 19 lieutenant colonels, 9 majors, and 29 captains.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup> By March 2007, about half of the Brigade had died.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In April 2010, the Cuban Pilot's Association unveiled a monument at the <a href="/wiki/Kendall-Tamiami_Executive_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Kendall-Tamiami Executive Airport">Kendall-Tamiami Executive Airport</a> in memory of the 16 aviators for the exile side killed during the battle.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup> The memorial consists of an <a href="/wiki/Obelisk" title="Obelisk">obelisk</a> and a restored B-26 replica aircraft atop a large <a href="/wiki/Cuban_flag" class="mw-redirect" title="Cuban flag">Cuban flag</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Spanish_term_for_the_event">Spanish term for the event</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bay_of_Pigs_Invasion&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Spanish term for the event">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The name for the invasion in Spanish faces political contestations. The Cuban government generally calls it "Playa Girón," while Cuban Americans and ordinary Hispanic Americans generally call it "Bahía de Cochinos".<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="American_public_reaction">American public reaction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bay_of_Pigs_Invasion&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: American public reaction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Only 3 percent of Americans supported military action in 1960.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_201-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-201">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup> According to Gallup, 72% of people had a negative view of Fidel Castro in 1960.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_201-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-201">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup> After the conflict, 61% of Americans approved of the action, while 15% disapproved and 24% were unsure. This poll was taken by Gallup in late April 1966.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup> A week after the invasion of Cuba, Gallup took another series of polls to sample three possible ways of opposing Castro.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup> The policy that most resembled the Bay of Pigs (if the US "should aid the anti-Castro forces with money and war materials") was still favored by a narrow margin, 44% approval to 41% rejecting this policy.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Kennedy's general approval rating actually increased in the first survey after the invasion, rising from 78 percent in mid-April to 83 percent in late April and early May.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup> Dr. Gallup's headline for this poll read, "Public Rallies Behind Kennedy in Aftermath of Cuban Crisis." In 1963 a public opinion poll showed 60 percent of Americans believed that Cuba is "a serious threat to world peace," yet, 63 percent of Americans did not want the US to remove Castro.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_201-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-201">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_surviving_veterans_of_the_Bay_of_Pigs_Invasion">Notable surviving veterans of the Bay of Pigs Invasion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bay_of_Pigs_Invasion&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Notable surviving veterans of the Bay of Pigs Invasion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Basulto" title="José Basulto">José Basulto</a> (b. 1940)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ricardo_Montero_Duque" title="Ricardo Montero Duque">Ricardo Montero Duque</a> (b. 1925)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Alfredo_Duran" title="Alfredo Duran">Alfredo Duran</a> (b. 1936)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Francisco_Jose_Hernandez" title="Francisco Jose Hernandez">Francisco Jose Hernandez</a> (b. 1936)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jose_Antonio_Llama" title="Jose Antonio Llama">Jose Antonio Llama</a> (b. 1941)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Erneido_Oliva" title="Erneido Oliva">Erneido Oliva</a> (b. 1932)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/F%C3%A9lix_Rodr%C3%ADguez_(soldier)" title="Félix Rodríguez (soldier)">Félix Rodríguez</a> (b. 1941)</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bay_of_Pigs_Invasion&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="navigation" aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright" style="margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em;border:solid #aaa 1px">
<ul style="display:table;box-sizing:border-box;padding:0.1em;max-width:175px;background:#f9f9f9;font-size:85%;line-height:110%;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold">
<li style="display:table-row"><span style="display:table-cell;padding:0.2em;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center"><img alt="flag" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Flag_of_Cuba.svg/32px-Flag_of_Cuba.svg.png" decoding="async" width="32" height="16" class="noviewer thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Flag_of_Cuba.svg/48px-Flag_of_Cuba.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Flag_of_Cuba.svg/64px-Flag_of_Cuba.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="600" /></span><span style="display:table-cell;padding:0.2em 0.2em 0.2em 0.3em;vertical-align:middle"><a href="/wiki/Portal:Cuba" title="Portal:Cuba">Cuba portal</a></span></li>
<li style="display:table-row"><span style="display:table-cell;padding:0.2em;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center"><img alt="flag" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/32px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" decoding="async" width="32" height="17" class="noviewer thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/48px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/64px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1235" data-file-height="650" /></span><span style="display:table-cell;padding:0.2em 0.2em 0.2em 0.3em;vertical-align:middle"><a href="/wiki/Portal:United_States" title="Portal:United States">United States portal</a></span></li>
<li style="display:table-row"><span style="display:table-cell;padding:0.2em;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Bluetank.png/32px-Bluetank.png" decoding="async" width="32" height="19" class="noviewer" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Bluetank.png/48px-Bluetank.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Bluetank.png/64px-Bluetank.png 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="237" /></span><span style="display:table-cell;padding:0.2em 0.2em 0.2em 0.3em;vertical-align:middle"><a href="/wiki/Portal:War" title="Portal:War">War portal</a></span></li></ul></div>
<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em;">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Cuban_Missile_Crisis" title="Cuban Missile Crisis">Cuban Missile Crisis</a> (1962)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cuba%E2%80%93United_States_relations" title="Cuba–United States relations">Cuba–United States relations</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cuban_Project" title="Cuban Project">Cuban Project</a> (Operation Mongoose, 1961–1965)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cuban_Revolution" title="Cuban Revolution">Cuban Revolution</a> (1959)</li>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Explanatory_notes">Explanatory notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bay_of_Pigs_Invasion&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Explanatory notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div style=""><ol class="references" style="list-style-type:upper-alpha;">
<li id="cnote_A"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#ref_A_1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">
Across the country
</span></li>
<li id="cnote_B"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#ref_B_1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">
1,500 ground forces (including 177 paratroops) – c. 1,300 landed. Also Cuban exile aircrews, American aircrews, CIA operatives<sup id="cite_ref-fernandez_40-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fernandez-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>
</span></li>
<li id="cnote_C"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#ref_C_1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">
176 Cuban government forces killed<sup id="cite_ref-fernandez_40-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fernandez-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-triay_123-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-triay-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup>
</span></li>
<li id="cnote_D"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#ref_D_1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">
500 Cuban forces wounded,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERodríguez1999180_206-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERodríguez1999180-206">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup> or 4,000 killed, missing or wounded (includes militias and armed civilians)<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup>
</span></li>
<li id="cnote_E"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#ref_E_1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">
118 invaders killed (114 Cuban exiles plus 4 American aircrew)<sup id="cite_ref-wyden_104-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wyden-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>
</span></li>
<li id="cnote_F"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#ref_F_1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">
1,202 Brigade members captured (1,179 tried; 14 tried previously for pre-invasion crimes; 9 died in transit)<sup id="cite_ref-fernandez_40-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fernandez-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>
</span></li>
</ol></div>

<li id="cite_note-109"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-109">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">British Foreign Office. Chancery American Department, Foreign Office, London 2 September 1959 (2181/59) to British Embassy Havana classified as restricted Released 2000 by among British Foreign Office papers. Foreign Offices Files for Cuba Part 1: Revolution in Cuba "in our letter 1011/59 May 6 we mentioned that a Russian workers' delegation had been invited to participate in the May Day celebrations here, but had been delayed. The interpreter with the party, which arrived later and stayed in Cuba a few days, was called Vadim Kotchergin although he was at the time using what he subsequently claimed was his mother's name of Liston (?). He remained in the background, and did not attract any attention". These two agents went on to train overseas personnel including Carlos the Jackal (Ilich Ramírez Sánchez) and subcomandante Marcos (Rafael Sebastián Guillén).</span>

<ul><li><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/List_of_presidents_of_the_United_States" title="List of presidents of the United States">35th</a> <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">President of the United States</a> (1961–1963)</span></li>
